  • The analysis of the transcriptomic data generated from the Zn shift focused on the role of ten key regulators : ArsR , BaeR , CpxR , CusR , Fur , OxyR , SoxS , ZntR , ZraR and Zur . [22016571]
  • They are involved in processes as diverse as respiration , gene regulation , cofactor biosynthesis , and DNA-RNA metabolism .7 There is tremendous interest in understanding the mechanisms of Fe-S cluster biosynthesis , one reason being that several human diseases , including Friedreich 's ataxia , are the result of genetic defects in the protein machinery that makes Fe-S clusters .7 10.1021 / pr100920r 2010 American Chemical Society 6740 Journal of Proteome Research 2010 , 9 , 6740 -- 6751 Published on Web 10/11/201 The SUF system of E. coli is comprised of complex protein machinery , which , under the control of OxyR , IHF , IscR , andFur , synthesizes Fe S clusters during the potentially cytotoxic conditions of iron limitation and oxidative-stress .6,11 -14 ,17,18 The SUF system is encoded by the sufABCDSE operon .14 SufS is a cysteine desulfurase that mobilizes inorganic sulfur via a pyridoxal-5 ′ - phosphate cofactor and a conserved cysteine ( C ) residue and transfers the sulfur atom through a proposed persulﬁde transfer mechanism to the conserved C51 residue on the sulfur acceptor protein SufE.19-21 SufB , SufC , and SufD form a complex ( SufBC2D , hereafter referred to as SufBCD ) 22 that stimulates this cysteine desulfurase activity through an unknown mechanism ,21 though SufC is known to be an atypical ABC transporter ATPase .12 In vitro evidence suggests that SufE transfers the sulfur atom to SufB within the SufBCD complex and that SufBCD acts as a scaffold upon which an Fe-S cluster is assembled.22-24 It is not known whether the persulﬁde sulfur on SufE is liberated via nucleophilic attack by the recipient Cys thiol on the terminal sulfur of the persulﬁde , which would result in persulﬁde transfer , or via nucleophilic attack on the bridging sulfur , which would produce a disulﬁde-linked complex between SufE and the recipient protein and liberate sulﬁde that may then bind a free Cys residue for use in assembling an Fe-S cluster .5 It also remains to be determined whether the assembled cluster on SufBCD is transferred to a target apoprotein directly or via SufA.22,25-27 It is possible that SufE transfers sulfur to proteins other than SufB , as both the iron source and the means by which the sulfur on SufE is incorporated into an Fe-S cluster remain unknown . [20936830]

  • In E coli , intracellular H2O2 stress activates the OxyR transcription factor , which then directly stimulates synthesis of approximately two dozen proteins ( Zheng et al. , 2001 ) . [19400769]
  • Many of the proteins involved in protection against H2O2 stress are positively regulated by the OxyR transcription factor , which is fully activated by the H2O2 that accumulates in Hpx − mutants ( Zheng et al. , 2001 ) . [21338418]

  • The induction of mntH is especially pronounced during during H2O2 stress , since OxyR directly activates its transcription ( Kehres et al. , 2002 ; Anjem et al. , 2009 ) . [21338418]
  • Upon oxidation , OxyR becomes a transcriptional-activator for multiple genes involved in the protection against oxidative-stress ( Christman et al. , 1989 ; Zheng et al. , 1998 ) . [10692164]
  • Under conditions of oxidative-stress , OxyR undergoes reversible formation of a disulphide bond , allowing it to activate the transcription of genes required for oxidative-stress defence ( Zheng et al. , 1998 ) . [11972787]
  • Escherichia coli cells utilize two transcription factors OxyR and SoxR to sense the oxidants and then induce various genes against oxidative-stress that are involved in removing oxidants , repairing damaged cell components and maintaining reducing conditions in the cell ( Bauer et al. , 1999 ; Storz and Imlay , 1999 ; Pomposiello and Demple , 2001 ) . [12773378]

  • DISCUSSION We have shown here ( i ) that E. coli maintains the intracellular concentration of H2O2 within a surprisingly narrow range ( ; 0.2 mM ) although the metabolic generation of H2O2 varies .10 - fold during growth ; ( ii ) that a signiﬁcant amount of this homeostatic control during exponential-growth seems to be accomplished by the transcriptional regulation of the katG-encoded HP-I ; ( iii ) that the variation of HP-I catalase levels reﬂects a continuous variation in the degree of OxyR activation ; ( iv ) that the protective role of OxyR activation is a pop-ulation-wide phenomenon , rather than one restricted to occasional cells undergoing more intense oxidative-stress ; ( v ) that the physiological trigger point for OxyR seems to lie at ; 0.2 mM , the level above which katG up-regulation is observed ; and ( vi ) that ahpFC plays an antimutator role but does not regulate H2O2 levels .   • To determine whether the observed repression in the OFF cells can be mediated by oxidized OxyR , we examined in vitro the interactions of oxidized OxyR with agn43 regulatory region DNA . [12644490]
  • We previously reported that the reduced form of OxyR is sufﬁcient for repression of transcription of agn43 from unmethylated template DNA , which is essential for deoxyadenosine methylase ( Dam ) - and OxyR-dependent phase variation of agn43 . [12644490]
  • In vitro transcription from an unmethylated template was repressed by OxyR ( C199S ) , which resembles the reduced form of OxyR . [12029051]
  • OxyR ( C199S ) resembles the reduced form of OxyR in DNA binding and regulatory properties , binds unmethylated agn43 DNA in vitro , and is sufﬁcient to repress agn43 transcription in vivo ( 15 , 42 ) . [12029051]
  • It was previously shown that oxidized OxyR binds to unmethylated agn43 DNA in vitro ( 7 , 12 ) , but its role in agn43 regulation was not addressed further . [12644490]
  • Neither the oxidized nor reduced form of OxyR could bind to the methylated agn43 template . [12644490]

  • In vitro , both oxidized OxyR and OxyR ( C199S ) , which is locked in the reduced conformation , bound to the agn regulatory region , but methylation of the three GATC sequences abrogated this binding . [10692164]
  • As aerobically prepared OxyR ( WT ) is in the oxidized state and OxyR ( C199S ) is locked in the reduced conformation , these data indicate that both the oxidized and the reduced forms of OxyR bind to non-methylated agn regulatory region DNA . [10692164]

  • They are involved in processes as diverse as respiration , gene regulation , cofactor biosynthesis , and DNA-RNA metabolism .7 There is tremendous interest in understanding the mechanisms of Fe-S cluster biosynthesis , one reason being that several human diseases , including Friedreich 's ataxia , are the result of genetic defects in the protein machinery that makes Fe-S clusters .7 10.1021 / pr100920r 2010 American Chemical Society 6740 Journal of Proteome Research 2010 , 9 , 6740 -- 6751 Published on Web 10/11/201 The SUF system of E. coli is comprised of complex protein machinery , which , under the control of OxyR , IHF , IscR , andFur , synthesizes Fe S clusters during the potentially cytotoxic conditions of iron limitation and oxidative stress.6,11-14 ,17,18 The SUF system is encoded by the sufABCDSE operon .14 SufS is a cysteine desulfurase that mobilizes inorganic sulfur via a pyridoxal-5 ′ - phosphate cofactor and a conserved cysteine ( C ) residue and transfers the sulfur atom through a proposed persulﬁde transfer mechanism to the conserved C51 residue on the sulfur acceptor protein SufE.19-21 SufB , SufC , and SufD form a complex ( SufBC2D , hereafter referred to as SufBCD ) 22 that stimulates this cysteine desulfurase activity through an unknown mechanism ,21 though SufC is known to be an atypical ABC transporter ATPase .12 In vitro evidence suggests that SufE transfers the sulfur atom to SufB within the SufBCD complex and that SufBCD acts as a scaffold upon which an Fe-S cluster is assembled.22-24 It is not known whether the persulﬁde sulfur on SufE is liberated via nucleophilic attack by the recipient Cys thiol on the terminal sulfur of the persulﬁde , which would result in persulﬁde transfer , or via nucleophilic attack on the bridging sulfur , which would produce a disulﬁde-linked complex between SufE and the recipient protein and liberate sulﬁde that may then bind a free Cys residue for use in assembling an Fe-S cluster .5 It also remains to be determined whether the assembled cluster on SufBCD is transferred to a target apoprotein directly or via SufA.22,25-27 It is possible that SufE transfers sulfur to proteins other than SufB , as both the iron source and the means by which the sulfur on SufE is incorporated into an Fe-S cluster remain unknown .   • Oxidized OxyR-DNA Contacts To examine the OxyR-DNA contacts , we analyzed the binding of oxidized OxyR to the natural oxyRS , katG , and ahpC sites with hydroxyl radical footprinting and missing nucleoside interference assays . [8087856]
  • Redox-Dependent Repositioning of DNA Contacts The hydroxyl radical interference assays presented here demonstrate that OxyR shifts its DNA contacts between oxidizingand reducing conditions and that the two forms of OxyR require different contacts for binding . [8087856]
  • This suggestion is based on the observations that the OxyR motif shows 2-fold dyad symmetry and that OxyR has a single helix-turn-helixDNA-binding domain that is unlikely to span two helical turns . [8087856]
  • The motif shows 2-fold symmetry , and the spacing of the ATAG elements suggests that OxyR contacts four helical turns . [8087856]
  • Fourth , the clusters of missing nucleosides on the two strands lie across from each other in the major groove ( see Figure 4 ) , suggesting that OxyR contacts bases in the major groove . [8087856]
  • In addition , ~ repressor contacts five to seven nucleotides in each region , while OxyR only contacts one to three nucleotides in each region . [8087856]
  • We suggest that the oxidized OxyR protein is a dimer of dimers and that each of the four subunits contacts one of the four major grooves ( illustrated in Figure 8 ) . [8087856]
  • We suggest that when OxyR alters its DNA contacts upon oxidation , two of the subunits remain bound while the other two subunits are simply shifted one helical turn ( so that subunits bound at grooves 4 and 5 are shifted to grooves 3 and 4 , respectively ) . [8087856]
  • In contrast , reduced OxyR contacts ATAGnT elements in two pairs of major grooves separated by one turn of the DNA helix ( Toledano et al. , 1994 ) . [17464064]
  • In contrast , reduced OxyR contacts two pairs of adjacent major grooves separated by one helical turn . [8087856]
  • This pattern of protection further supports the conclusion that oxidized OxyR binds to four major grooves protecting the five adjacent minor grooves . [8087856]
  • Third , the missing nucleosides are located approximately 10 bp apart , parallel to the helical axis of the DNA , implying that OxyR binds on one face of the helix in four successive grooves . [8087856]
  • Here , we report that oxidized OxyR recognizes a motif comprised of four ATAGnt elements spaced at 10 bp intervals and contacts these elements in four adjacent major grooves on one face of the DNA helix . [8087856]
  • These experiments revealed that oxidized OxyR binds to an ATAGnt motif on one face of the DNA helix at four adjacent major grooves . [8087856]
  • Speciﬁcally , in the presence of hydrogen peroxide , OxyR becomes oxidized , which results in a change in its structure , which in turn contributes to a change in protein-DNA contacts . [12029051]
  • Second , the critical contacts defined by the interference assays map to the four ATAGnt boxes that define the OxyR motif , supporting the conclusion that OxyR contacts the DNA at these sequences . [8087856]
  • We propose that specific DNA-recognition by an OxyR tetramer is achieved with four contacts of intermediate affinity allowing OxyR to reposition its DNA contacts and target alternate sets of promoters as the cellular redox state is altered . [8087856]
  • Therefore , we propose that oxidized OxyR achieves tight specific binding by th combination of four contacts of intermediate affinity , rather than by two contacts of high affinity as seen for many of the helix-turn-helixproteins . [8087856]
  • While repressor contacts DNA in two regions , OxyR makes contacts in four regions . [8087856]
  • These patterns are consistent with our suggestion that OxyR makes four intermediate strength contacts , while the repressor binds to DNA with two strong contacts . [8087856]

  • Michael acceptor sites are apparently not involved in the modification , but rather the reactive ( electrophilic ) carbonyl group of the outer monoterpene side chain ( structure I ) subserves transesterification ( oxyester 3 thioester ) of OxyR cysteine thiol . [16030151]
  • For example , the reaction of hydrogen peroxide with nucleophilic cysteine residue sulfhydryls in the transcription regulators OxyR and OhrR of bacteria and Orp1 of Saccharomyces cerevisiae generates cysteine sulfenic acid ( R-S-OH ) , an intermediate that initiates a series of events leading to expression of antioxidant genes .2,3 Many of these cysteine residue sulfhydryls have been shown to have a pKa below that of free cysteine ( 8.3 ) , suggesting that low pKa cysteine residues are redox active .2,4 Sulfur trafﬁcking pathways are among the systems that are induced during oxidative stress , and these pathways also use nucleo-philic cysteine residue sulfhydryls.5-7 In the ﬁrst step of sulfur trafﬁcking , a cysteine desulfurase abstracts inorganic sulfur from the cysteine substrate using its own reactive cysteine residue sulfhydryl , thereby forming a persulﬁde ( R-S-SH ) intermediate . [20936830]
  • Bacterial OxyR shares some similarities with mammalian Nrf2 : both regulate the expression of detoxifying enzymes and antioxidant proteins , both contain critical Cys residues that serve sensory and regulatory roles , and both are activated by peroxides . [16030151]
  • Mass spectrometric analysis of activated OxyR revealed thioesteriﬁcation of the critical regulatory cysteine , Cys-199 , to an avicin fragment comprising the outer monoterpene side chain . [16030151]
  • To determine whether the cysteine residues in OxyR were important for sensing the oxidative stress signal , we changed each of the six cysteines to serine by site-directed mutagenesis . [7868602]
  • Using site-directed mutagenesis , we found that one cysteine residue ( C-199 ) is critical for the redox sensitivity of OxyR , and a C-1993S mutation appears to lock the OxyR protein in the reduced form . [7868602]
  • Using site-directed mutagenesis , we found that only one ( C-199 ) of six cysteine resi-dues was critical for the induction of defense genes by OxyR . [7868602]
  • The six possible redox-reactive cysteines in OxyR were mutagenized to serine , and a single cysteine ( Cys-199 ) was found to be critical for activity . [7868602]
  • Each OxyR monomer has six cysteine residues , of which only Cys-199 is essential for regulation by redox agents ( 21 ) . [16030151]
  • It may be significant that none ofthe six cysteine residues found in the OxyR protein is present in LysR or NodD since cysteines might easily be oxidized . [2471187]
  • Most protein cysteine residues react far too sluggishly to be affected by micromolar H2O2 , but the OxyR , AhpC , and OhrR proteins feature active-site cysteines that are activated by local context so they are easily oxidized to sulfenic acid ( Imlay , 2008a ) . [21143317]
  • In addition , a mutant form of OxyR in which five of the six cysteine residues have been induction of converted to serine shows wild-type oxyR-regulated genes in vivo ( 15 ) . [2183352]

  • For many years , OxyR had been thought to contain only one essential cysteine residue ( Cys199 ) whose oxidation to a sulfenic acid was solely responsible for sensing and activating the response to hydrogen peroxide ( Storz et al. , 1990 ; Kullik et al. , 1995 ) However , it is now clear that OxyR has two essential cysteines , Cysl99 and Cys208 , and that the hydrogen peroxide response involves Cys 199 oxidation to a sulfenic acid followed by the formation of an intramolecular disulfide bridge with Cys208 . [11407111]
  • Most data support a model in which the peroxide-mediated oxidative stress signal is transduced by oxidation of two cysteine residues in OxyR , which leads to the formation of an intramolecular disulﬁde bridge . [12644490]

  • DISCUSSION The cloning and DNA sequence of the E. coli oxyR gene , a positive regulator of a regulon for defenses against oxidative stress , revealed that OxyR is a 34-kDa protein that shows significant homology to a family of bacterial regulatory proteins . [2471187]
  • OxyR protein is a positive regulator for a number of genes induced by oxidative stresses and , consistent with this , an homology search revealed that the protein is homologous to a large family of bacterial activator proteins . [2511419]
  • Here we report that OxyR is a member of a family of bacterial regulator proteins . [2471187]
  • In the N-terminal highly homologous region , the sequence of 20 amino acids of OxyR protein ( residues 18-37 ) is similar to a helix-turn-helix motif of DNA binding proteins ( Pabo and Sauer 1984 ) ( Fig. 7 ) . [2511419]
  • An interesting feature of this region was the nucleotide sequence homology ( 39.5 % identity ) shared between it and the promoter regions of the mom and oxyR genes , both of which are known to bind OxyR , a LysR-type transcriptional activator ( 12 , 22 ) . [10094691]
  • This region shows the highest degree of amino acid sequence similarity among family members and is believed to participate in DNA-binding according to mutational studies performed on several LTTRs , e.g. NahR ( Schell et al. , 1990 ) , OxyR ( et al. , 1995a ) , GcvA ( Jourdan and Stauffer , 1998 ) , CysB ( Lochowska et al. , 2001 ) and CrgA ( Deghmane and Taha , 2003 ) . [15255893]
  • These results suggest that the Nterminal region of OxyR is involved in DNA binding , similarly to those of the other nine members of the family ( Hen-ikoff et al. 1988 ) . [2511419]
  • The structures of the cofactor-binding domains of two family members , CysB and OxyR , have been solved by X-ray crystallography ( Tyrrell et al. , 1997 ; Choi et al. , 2001 ) . [15255893]
  • A DNase I hypersensitive site was also previously seen for IlvY ( a member of the family of regulators showing homology to OxyR ) in the absence but not in the presence of the inducer of the IlvY-mediated response ( 22 ) . [2183352]
  • Some of the other bacterial regulators that show homology to OxyR have also been found to be bound to the promoters that they regulate in both the presence and absence of inducer ( 22 , 24 ) suggesting that members of this family of regulators may all be ideally designed for responses requiring immediate induction . [2183352]

  • They are involved in processes as diverse as respiration , gene regulation , cofactor-biosynthesis , and DNA-RNA-metabolism .7 There is tremendous interest in understanding the mechanisms of Fe-S cluster biosynthesis , one reason being that several human diseases , including Friedreich 's ataxia , are the result of genetic defects in the protein machinery that makes Fe-S clusters .7 10.1021 / pr100920r 2010 American Chemical Society 6740 Journal of Proteome Research 2010 , 9 , 6740 -- 6751 Published on Web 10/11/201 The SUF system of E. coli is comprised of complex protein machinery , which , under the control of OxyR , IHF , IscR , andFur , synthesizes Fe S clusters during the potentially cytotoxic conditions of iron limitation and oxidative stress.6,11-14 ,17,18 The SUF system is encoded by the sufABCDSE operon .14 SufS is a cysteine desulfurase that mobilizes inorganic sulfur via a pyridoxal-5 ′ - phosphate cofactor and a conserved cysteine ( C ) residue and transfers the sulfur atom through a proposed persulﬁde transfer mechanism to the conserved C51 residue on the sulfur acceptor protein SufE.19-21 SufB , SufC , and SufD form a complex ( SufBC2D , hereafter referred to as SufBCD ) 22 that stimulates this cysteine desulfurase activity through an unknown mechanism ,21 though SufC is known to be an atypical ABC transporter ATPase .12 In vitro evidence suggests that SufE transfers the sulfur atom to SufB within the SufBCD complex and that SufBCD acts as a scaffold upon which an Fe-S cluster is assembled.22-24 It is not known whether the persulﬁde sulfur on SufE is liberated via nucleophilic attack by the recipient Cys thiol on the terminal sulfur of the persulﬁde , which would result in persulﬁde transfer , or via nucleophilic attack on the bridging sulfur , which would produce a disulﬁde-linked complex between SufE and the recipient protein and liberate sulﬁde that may then bind a free Cys residue for use in assembling an Fe-S cluster .5 It also remains to be determined whether the assembled cluster on SufBCD is transferred to a target apoprotein directly or via SufA.22,25-27 It is possible that SufE transfers sulfur to proteins other than SufB , as both the iron source and the means by which the sulfur on SufE is incorporated into an Fe-S cluster remain unknown . [20936830]

  • For example , the reaction of hydrogen peroxide with nucleophilic cysteine residue sulfhydryls in the transcription regulators OxyR and OhrR of bacteria and Orp1 of Saccharomyces cerevisiae generates cysteine sulfenic acid ( R-S-OH ) , an intermediate that initiates a series of events leading to expression of antioxidant genes .2,3 Many of these cysteine residue sulfhydryls have been shown to have a pKa below that of free cysteine ( 8.3 ) , suggesting that low pKa cysteine residues are redox active .2,4 Sulfur trafﬁcking pathways are among the systems that are induced during oxidative stress , and these pathways also use nucleo-philic cysteine residue sulfhydryls.5-7 In the ﬁrst step of sulfur trafﬁcking , a cysteine desulfurase abstracts inorganic sulfur from the cysteine substrate using its own reactive cysteine residue sulfhydryl , thereby forming a persulﬁde ( R-S-SH ) intermediate .   • For example , the reaction of hydrogen peroxide with nucleophilic cysteine residue sulfhydryls in the transcription regulators OxyR and OhrR of bacteria and Orp1 of Saccharomyces cerevisiae generates cysteine sulfenic acid ( R-S-OH ) , an intermediate that initiates a series of events leading to expression of antioxidant genes .2,3 Many of these cysteine residue sulfhydryls have been shown to have a pKa below that of free cysteine ( 8.3 ) , suggesting that low pKa cysteine residues are redox active .2,4 Sulfur trafﬁcking pathways are among the systems that are induced during oxidative stress , and these pathways also use nucleo-philic cysteine residue sulfhydryls.5-7 In the ﬁrst step of sulfur trafﬁcking , a cysteine desulfurase abstracts inorganic sulfur from the cysteine substrate using its own reactive cysteine residue sulfhydryl , thereby forming a persulﬁde ( R-S-SH ) intermediate .
